&confProto.GetConfigResponse{RawUnified: raw.ToProto()}, nil\n   427→}\n   428→\n   429→// newInternalHTTPHandler creates and returns the HTTP handler for the internal API (accessible to\n   430→// other internal services).\n   431→func newInternalHTTPHandler(\n   432→\tschema *graphql.Schema,\n   433→\tdb database.DB,\n   434→\tgitserverClient gitserver.Client,\n   435→\tnewCodeIntelUploadHandler enterprise.NewCodeIntelUploadHandler,\n   436→\tnewComputeStreamHandler enterprise.NewComputeStreamHandler,\n   437→) http.Handler {\n   438→\tinternalMux := http.NewServeMux()\n   439→\tlogger := log.Scoped(\"internal\")\n   440→\n   441→\tinternalRouter := httpapi.NewInternalServicesRouter(\n   442→\t\tdb,\n   443→\t\tgitserverClient,\n   444→\t\tschema,\n   445→\t\tnewCodeIntelUploadHandler,\n   446→\t\tnewComputeStreamHandler,\n   447→\t)\n   448→\n   449→\tinternalMux.Handle(\"/.internal/\", internalRouter)\n   450→\n   451→\th := http.Handler(internalMux)\n   452→\th = featureflag.Middleware(db.FeatureFlags(), h)\n   453→\th = actor.HTTPMiddleware(logger, h)\n   454→\th = tenant.InternalHTTPMiddleware(logger, h)\n   455→\th = gzhttp.GzipHandler(h)\n   456→\th = tracepkg.HTTPMiddleware(logger, h)\n   457→\th = instrumentation.HTTPMiddleware(\"internal\", h)\n   458→\treturn h\n   459→}\n   460→\n   461→// corsAllowHeader is the HTTP header that, if present (and assuming secureHeadersMiddleware is\n   462→// used), indicates that the incoming HTTP request is either same-origin or is from an allowed\n   463→// origin. See\n   464→// https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Cross-Site_Request_Forgery_(CSRF)_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet#Protecting_REST_Services:_Use_of_Custom_Request_Headers\n   465→// for more information on this technique.\n   466→const corsAllowHeader = \"X-Requested-With\"\n   467→\n   468→// crossOriginPolicy describes the cross-origin policy the middleware should be enforcing.\n   469→type crossOriginPolicy string\n   470→\n   471→const (\n   472→\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests as a\n   473→\t// public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain but\n   474→\t// cookie/session-based authentication is only allowed if the origin is in the configured\n   475→\t// allow-list of origins. Otherwise, only access token authentication is permitted.\n   476→\t//\n   477→\t// This is to be used for all /.api routes, such as our GraphQL and search streaming APIs as we\n   478→\t// want third-party websites (such as e.g. github1s.com, or internal tools for on-prem\n   479→\t// customers) to be able to leverage our API. Their users will need to provide an access token,\n   480→\t// or the website would need to be added to Sourcegraph's CORS allow list in order to be granted\n   481→\t// cookie/session-based authentication (which is dangerous to expose to untrusted domains.)\n   482→\tcrossOriginPolicyAPI crossOriginPolicy = \"API\"\n   483→\n   484→\t// crossOriginPolicyAssets describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests to\n   485→\t// static resources as a public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain.\n   486→\t//\n   487→\t// This is to be used for static assets served from the /.assets route. For example, using this\n   488→\t// route, the Phabricator native extension loads styles via the fetch interface.\n   489→\tcrossOriginPolicyAssets crossOriginPolicy = \"assets\"\n   490→\n   491→\t// crossOriginPolicyNever describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests by\n   492→\t// never allowing them. This makes sense for e.g. routes such as e.g. sign out pages, where\n   493→\t// cookie based authentication is needed and requests should never come from a domain other than\n   494→\t// the Sourcegraph instance itself.\n   495→\t//\n   496→\t// Important: This only applies to cross-origin requests issued by clients that respect CORS,\n   497→\t// such as browsers. So for example Code Intelligence /.executors, despite being \"an API\",\n   498→\t// should use this policy unless they intend to get cross-origin requests _from browsers_.\n   499→\tcrossOriginPolicyNever crossOriginPolicy = \"never\"\n   500→)\n   501→\n   502→// secureHeadersMiddleware adds and checks for HTTP security-related headers.\n   503→//\n   504→// 🚨 SECURITY: This handler is served to all clients, even on private servers to clients who have\n   505→// not authenticated. It must not reveal any sensitive information.\n   506→func secureHeadersMiddleware(logger log.Logger, db database.DB, next http.Handler, policy crossOriginPolicy) http.Handler {\n   507→\treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n   508→\t\t// headers for security\n   509→\t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-Content-Type-Options\", \"nosniff\")\n   510→\t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-XSS-Protection\", \"1; mode=block\")\n   511→\t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-Frame-Options\", \"DENY\")\n   512→\t\t// no cache by default\n   513→\t\tw.Header().Set(\"Cache-Control\", \"no-cache, max-age=0\")\n   514→\n   515→\t\t// Write CORS headers and potentially handle the requests if it is an OPTIONS request.\n   516→\t\tif handled := handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin(logger, db), w, r, policy); handled {\n   517→\t\t\treturn // request was handled, do not invoke next handler\n   518→\t\t}\n   519→\n   520→\t\tnext.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n   521→\t})\n   522→}\n   523→\n   524→// handleCORSRequest handles checking the Origin header and writing CORS Access-Control-Allow-*\n   525→// headers. In some cases, it may handle OPTIONS CORS preflight requests in which case the function\n   526→// returns true and the request should be considered fully served.\n   527→func handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin func(context.Context, string) bool, w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request, policy crossOriginPolicy) (handled bool) {\n   528→\t// If this route is one which should never allow cross-origin requests, then we should return\n   529→\t// early. We do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browsers\n   530→\t// default (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\n   531→\t//\n   532→\t// We could instead parse the domain from conf.Get().ExternalURL and use that in the response,\n   533→\t// to make things more explicit, but it would add more logic here to think about and you would\n   534→\t// also want to think about whether or not `OPTIONS` requests should be handled and if the other\n   535→\t// headers (-Credentials, -Methods, -Headers, etc.) should be sent back in such a situation.\n   536→\t// Instead, it's easier to reason about the code by just saying \"we send back nothing in this\n   537→\t// case, and so the browser enforces no cross-origin requests\".\n   538→\t//\n   539→\t// This is in compliance with section 7.2 \"Resource Sharing Check\" of the CORS standard: https://www.w3.org/TR/2020/SPSD-cors-20200602/#resource-sharing-check-0\n   540→\t// It states:\n   541→\t//\n   542→\t// > If the response includes zero or more than one Access-Control-Allow-Origin header values,\n   543→\t// > return fail and terminate this algorithm.\n   544→\t//\n   545→\t// And you may also see the type of error the browser would produce in this instance at e.g.\n   546→\t// https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/CORS/Errors/CORSMissingAllowOrigin\n   547→\t//\n   548→\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyNever {\n   549→\t\treturn false\n   550→\t}\n   551→\n   552→\t// If the crossOriginPolicyAssets is used and the requested asset is not from the extension folder,\n   553→\t// we do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browser's default\n   554→\t// (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\n   555→\t//\n   556→\t// We allow cross-origin requests for assets in the `./client/web/dist/extension` folder because they\n   557→\t// are required for the native Phabricator extension.\n   558→\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyAssets && !strings.HasPrefix(r.URL.Path, \"/extension/\") {\n   559→\t\treturn false\n   560→\t}\n   561→\n   562→\t// Check Fetch metadata to determine request site, if the request is cross-site\n   563→\t// or the metadata doesn't exist we handle the request.\n   564→\tif reqSite := r.Header.Get(csrf.SecFetchSite); reqSite != \"\" && reqSite != \"cross-site\" {\n   565→\t\treturn false\n   566→\t}\n   567→\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI and crossOriginPolicyAssets - handling of API and static assets routes.\n   568→\t//\n   569→\t// Even if the request was not from a trusted origin, we will allow the browser to send it AND\n   570→\t// include credentials even. Traditionally, this would be a CSRF vulnerability! But because we\n   571→\t// know for a fact that we will only respect sessions (cookie-based-authentication) iff the\n   572→\t// request came from a trusted origin, in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety, we know it\n   573→\t// is safe to do this.\n   574→\t//\n   575→\t// This is the ONLY way in which we can enable public access of our Sourcegraph.com API, i.e. to\n   576→\t// allow random.com to send requests to our GraphQL and search APIs either unauthenticated or\n   577→\t// using an access token.\n   578→\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Credentials\", \"true\")\n   579→\n   580→\t// Note: This must mirror the request's `Origin` header exactly as API users rely on this\n   581→\t// codepath handling for example wildcards `*` and `null` origins properly. For example, if\n   582→\t// Sourcegraph is behind a corporate VPN an admin may choose to set the CORS origin to \"*\" (via\n   583→\t// a proxy, a browser would never send a literal \"*\") and would expect Sourcegraph to respond\n   584→\t// appropriately with the request's Origin header. Similarly, some environments issue requests\n   585→\t// with a `null` Origin header, such as VS Code extensions from within WebViews and Figma\n   586→\t// extensions. Thus:\n   587→\t//\n   588→\t// \t\"Origin: *\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *\"\n   589→\t// \t\"Origin: null\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: null\"\n   590→\t// \t\"Origin: https://foobar.com\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: https://foobar.com\"\n   591→\t//\n   592→\t// Again, this is fine because we allow API requests from any origin and instead prevent CSRF\n   593→\t// attacks via enforcing that we only respect session auth iff the origin is trusted. See the\n   594→\t// docstring above this one for more info.\n   595→\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin\", r.Header.Get(\"Origin\"))\n   596→\n   597→\tif r.Method == \"OPTIONS\" {\n   598→\t\t// CRITICAL: Only trusted origins are allowed to send the secure X-Requested-With and\n   599→\t\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client headers, which indicate to us later (in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety)\n   600→\t\t// that the request came from a trusted origin. To understand these secure headers, see\n   601→\t\t// \"What does X-Requested-With do anyway?\" in https://github.com/sourcegraph/sourcegraph-public-snapshot/pull/27931\n   602→\t\t//\n   603→\t\t// Any origin may send us POST, GET, OPTIONS requests with arbitrary content types, auth\n   604→\t\t// (session cookies and access tokens), etc. but only trusted origins may send us the secure\n   605→\t\t// X-Requested-With header.\n   606→\t\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Methods\", \"GET, POST, OPTIONS\")\n   607→\n   608→\t\theaders := []string{}\n   609→\n   610→\t\tif isTrustedOrigin(r.Context(), r.Header.Get(\"Origin\")) {\n   611→\t\t\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client is the deprecated form of X-Requested-With, so we treat it the same\n   612→\t\t\t// way. It is NOT respected anymore, but is left as an allowed header so as to not block\n   613→\t\t\t// requests that still do include it as e.g. part of a proxy put in front of Sourcegraph.\n   614→\t\t\theaders = append(headers, corsAllowHeader, \"X-Sourcegraph-Client\")\n   615→\t\t}\n   616→\n   617→\t\t// Add headers specified by the site config. Importantly, this list does _not_ include\n   635→\t\t// corsAllowHeader. The list is formatted for use with Access-Control-Allow-Headers.\n   636→\t\t//\n   637→\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace: indicates whether we should enable tracing for the request\n   638→\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name: contains a client-reported name for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n   639→\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version: contains a client-reported version for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n   640→\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature: contains a client reported feature for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n   641→\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID: reports an anonymous ID for clients that are not logged in. Used for event metadata unauthed dotcom users.\n   642→\t\tconst safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins = \"Content-Type, Authorization, X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature, X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID\"\n   643→\t\theaders = append(headers, safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins)\n   644→\n   645→\t\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Headers\", strings.Join(headers, \", \"))\n   646→\t\tw.WriteHeader(http.StatusOK)\n   647→\t\treturn true // we handled the request\n   648→\t}\n   649→\treturn false\n   650→}\n   651→\n   652→// isTrustedOrigin returns whether the HTTP request's Origin is trusted to\n   653→// initiate authenticated cross-origin requests.\n   654→func isTrustedOrigin(logger log.Logger, db database.DB) func(ctx context.Context, requestOrigin string) bool {\n   655→\treturn func(ctx context.Context, requestOrigin string) bool {\n   656→\t\tisExtensionRequest := requestOrigin == devExtension || requestOrigin == prodExtension\n   657→\n   658→\t\tvar isCORSAllowedRequest bool\n   659→\t\tif corsOrigin := conf.Get().CorsOrigin; Currently, this includes the conf server and the Zoekt indexer server.\nfunc newInternalGRPCServer(logger log.Logger, db database.DB, gitserverClient gitserver.Client) *grpc.Server {\n\tgrpcServer := defaults.NewServer(logger)\n\n\t// zoekt-indexserver endpoints\n\tzoektGitserverClient := gitserverClient.Scoped(\"zoektindexerserver\")\n\tindexer := httapisearch.NewSearchIndexerServer(\n\t\tdb,\n\t\tlogger,\n\t\tzoektGitserverClient,\n\t\tbackend.NewRepos(logger, db, zoektGitserverClient).ListIndexable,\n\t\tdb.Repos(),\n\t\tfunc(ctx context.Context, repoIDs []api.RepoID) (map[api.RepoID][]string, error) {\n\t\t\treturn searchcontexts.RepoRevs(ctx, db, repoIDs)\n\t\t},\n\t\tsearch.Indexers(db),\n\t\tos.Getenv(\"SRC_SEARCH_INDEXER_EFFICIENT_POLLING_DISABLED\") != \"\")\n\tzoektProto.RegisterZoektConfigurationServiceServer(grpcServer, httapisearch.NewSearchIndexerGRPCServer(indexer))\n\tconfProto.RegisterConfigServiceServer(grpcServer, &configServer{})\n\n\treturn grpcServer\n}\n\n// configServer implements proto.ConfigServiceServer to serve config to other clients in the cluster.\ntype configServer struct {\n\tconfProto.UnimplementedConfigServiceServer\n}\n\nfunc (c *configServer) GetConfig(_ context.Context, _ *confProto.GetConfigRequest) (*confProto.GetConfigResponse, error) {\n\traw := conf.Raw()\n\treturn &confProto.GetConfigResponse{RawUnified: raw.ToProto()}, nil\n}\n\n// newInternalHTTPHandler creates and returns the HTTP handler for the internal API (accessible to\n// other internal services).\nfunc newInternalHTTPHandler(\n\tschema *graphql.Schema,\n\tdb database.DB,\n\tgitserverClient gitserver.Client,\n\tnewCodeIntelUploadHandler enterprise.NewCodeIntelUploadHandler,\n\tnewComputeStreamHandler enterprise.NewComputeStreamHandler,\n) http.Handler {\n\tinternalMux := http.NewServeMux()\n\tlogger := log.Scoped(\"internal\")\n\n\tinternalRouter := httpapi.NewInternalServicesRouter(\n\t\tdb,\n\t\tgitserverClient,\n\t\tschema,\n\t\tnewCodeIntelUploadHandler,\n\t\tnewComputeStreamHandler,\n\t)\n\n\tinternalMux.Handle(\"/.internal/\", internalRouter)\n\n\th := http.Handler(internalMux)\n\th = featureflag.Middleware(db.FeatureFlags(), h)\n\th = actor.HTTPMiddleware(logger, h)\n\th = tenant.InternalHTTPMiddleware(logger, h)\n\th = gzhttp.GzipHandler(h)\n\th = tracepkg.HTTPMiddleware(logger, h)\n\th = instrumentation.HTTPMiddleware(\"internal\", h)\n\treturn h\n}\n\n// corsAllowHeader is the HTTP header that, if present (and assuming secureHeadersMiddleware is\n// used), indicates that the incoming HTTP request is either same-origin or is from an allowed\n// origin. See\n// https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Cross-Site_Request_Forgery_(CSRF)_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet#Protecting_REST_Services:_Use_of_Custom_Request_Headers\n// for more information on this technique.\nconst corsAllowHeader = \"X-Requested-With\"\n\n// crossOriginPolicy describes the cross-origin policy the middleware should be enforcing.\ntype crossOriginPolicy string\n\nconst (\n\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests as a\n\t// public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain but\n\t// cookie/session-based authentication is only allowed if the origin is in the configured\n\t// allow-list of origins. Otherwise, only access token authentication is permitted.\n\t//\n\t// This is to be used for all /.api routes, such as our GraphQL and search streaming APIs as we\n\t// want third-party websites (such as e.g. github1s.com, or internal tools for on-prem\n\t// customers) to be able to leverage our API. Their users will need to provide an access token,\n\t// or the website would need to be added to Sourcegraph's CORS allow list in order to be granted\n\t// cookie/session-based authentication (which is dangerous to expose to untrusted domains.)\n\tcrossOriginPolicyAPI crossOriginPolicy = \"API\"\n\n\t// crossOriginPolicyAssets describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests to\n\t// static resources as a public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain.\n\t//\n\t// This is to be used for static assets served from the /.assets route. For example, using this\n\t// route, the Phabricator native extension loads styles via the fetch interface.\n\tcrossOriginPolicyAssets crossOriginPolicy = \"assets\"\n\n\t// crossOriginPolicyNever describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests by\n\t// never allowing them. This makes sense for e.g. routes such as e.g. sign out pages, where\n\t// cookie based authentication is needed and requests should never come from a domain other than\n\t// the Sourcegraph instance itself.\n\t//\n\t// Important: This only applies to cross-origin requests issued by clients that respect CORS,\n\t// such as browsers. So for example Code Intelligence /.executors, despite being \"an API\",\n\t// should use this policy unless they intend to get cross-origin requests _from browsers_.\n\tcrossOriginPolicyNever crossOriginPolicy = \"never\"\n)\n\n// secureHeadersMiddleware adds and checks for HTTP security-related headers.\n//\n// 🚨 SECURITY: This handler is served to all clients, even on private servers to clients who have\n// not authenticated. It must not reveal any sensitive information.\nfunc secureHeadersMiddleware(logger log.Logger, db database.DB, next http.Handler, policy crossOriginPolicy) http.Handler {\n\treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n\t\t// headers for security\n\t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-Content-Type-Options\", \"nosniff\")\n\t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-XSS-Protection\", \"1; mode=block\")\n\t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-Frame-Options\", \"DENY\")\n\t\t// no cache by default\n\t\tw.Header().Set(\"Cache-Control\", \"no-cache, max-age=0\")\n\n\t\t// Write CORS headers and potentially handle the requests if it is an OPTIONS request.\n\t\tif handled := handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin(logger, db), w, r, policy); handled {\n\t\t\treturn // request was handled, do not invoke next handler\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tnext.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n\t})\n}\n\n// handleCORSRequest handles checking the Origin header and writing CORS Access-Control-Allow-*\n// headers. In some cases, it may handle OPTIONS CORS preflight requests in which case the function\n// returns true and the request should be considered fully served.\nfunc handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin func(context.Context, string) bool, w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request, policy crossOriginPolicy) (handled bool) {\n\t// If this route is one which should never allow cross-origin requests, then we should return\n\t// early. We do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browsers\n\t// default (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\n\t//\n\t// We could instead parse the domain from conf.Get().ExternalURL and use that in the response,\n\t// to make things more explicit, but it would add more logic here to think about and you would\n\t// also want to think about whether or not `OPTIONS` requests should be handled and if the other\n\t// headers (-Credentials, -Methods, -Headers, etc.) should be sent back in such a situation.\n\t// Instead, it's easier to reason about the code by just saying \"we send back nothing in this\n\t// case, and so the browser enforces no cross-origin requests\".\n\t//\n\t// This is in compliance with section 7.2 \"Resource Sharing Check\" of the CORS standard: https://www.w3.org/TR/2020/SPSD-cors-20200602/#resource-sharing-check-0\n\t// It states:\n\t//\n\t// > If the response includes zero or more than one Access-Control-Allow-Origin header values,\n\t// > return fail and terminate this algorithm.\n\t//\n\t// And you may also see the type of error the browser would produce in this instance at e.g.\n\t// https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/CORS/Errors/CORSMissingAllowOrigin\n\t//\n\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyNever {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// If the crossOriginPolicyAssets is used and the requested asset is not from the extension folder,\n\t// we do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browser's default\n\t// (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\n\t//\n\t// We allow cross-origin requests for assets in the `./client/web/dist/extension` folder because they\n\t// are required for the native Phabricator extension.\n\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyAssets && !strings.HasPrefix(r.URL.Path, \"/extension/\") {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// Check Fetch metadata to determine request site, if the request is cross-site\n\t// or the metadata doesn't exist we handle the request.\n\tif reqSite := r.Header.Get(csrf.SecFetchSite); reqSite != \"\" && reqSite != \"cross-site\" {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI and crossOriginPolicyAssets - handling of API and static assets routes.\n\t//\n\t// Even if the request was not from a trusted origin, we will allow the browser to send it AND\n\t// include credentials even. Traditionally, this would be a CSRF vulnerability! But because we\n\t// know for a fact that we will only respect sessions (cookie-based-authentication) iff the\n\t// request came from a trusted origin, in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety, we know it\n\t// is safe to do this.\n\t//\n\t// This is the ONLY way in which we can enable public access of our Sourcegraph.com API, i.e. to\n\t// allow random.com to send requests to our GraphQL and search APIs either unauthenticated or\n\t// using an access token.\n\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Credentials\", \"true\")\n\n\t// Note: This must mirror the request's `Origin` header exactly as API users rely on this\n\t// codepath handling for example wildcards `*` and `null` origins properly. For example, if\n\t// Sourcegraph is behind a corporate VPN an admin may choose to set the CORS origin to \"*\" (via\n\t// a proxy, a browser would never send a literal \"*\") and would expect Sourcegraph to respond\n\t// appropriately with the request's Origin header. Similarly, some environments issue requests\n\t// with a `null` Origin header, such as VS Code extensions from within WebViews and Figma\n\t// extensions. Thus:\n\t//\n\t// \t\"Origin: *\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *\"\n\t// \t\"Origin: null\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: null\"\n\t// \t\"Origin: https://foobar.com\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: https://foobar.com\"\n\t//\n\t// Again, this is fine because we allow API requests from any origin and instead prevent CSRF\n\t// attacks via enforcing that we only respect session auth iff the origin is trusted. See the\n\t// docstring above this one for more info.\n\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin\", r.Header.Get(\"Origin\"))\n\n\tif r.Method == \"OPTIONS\" {\n\t\t// CRITICAL: Only trusted origins are allowed to send the secure X-Requested-With and\n\t\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client headers, which indicate to us later (in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety)\n\t\t// that the request came from a trusted origin. To understand these secure headers, see\n\t\t// \"What does X-Requested-With do anyway?\" in https://github.com/sourcegraph/sourcegraph-public-snapshot/pull/27931\n\t\t//\n\t\t// Any origin may send us POST, GET, OPTIONS requests with arbitrary content types, auth\n\t\t// (session cookies and access tokens), etc. but only trusted origins may send us the secure\n\t\t// X-Requested-With header.\n\t\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Methods\", \"GET, POST, OPTIONS\")\n\n\t\theaders := []string{}\n\n\t\tif isTrustedOrigin(r.Context(), r.Header.Get(\"Origin\")) {\n\t\t\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client is the deprecated form of X-Requested-With, so we treat it the same\n\t\t\t// way. It is NOT respected anymore, but is left as an allowed header so as to not block\n\t\t\t// requests that still do include it as e.g. part of a proxy put in front of Sourcegraph.\n\t\t\theaders = append(headers, corsAllowHeader, \"X-Sourcegraph-Client\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Add headers specified by the site config. The site must be deployed behind a proxy which\n\t\t// manages its auth headers.\n\t\tif conf := conf.Get(); conf != nil && conf.AuthProviders != nil {\n\t\t\tfor _, p := range conf.AuthProviders {\n\t\t\t\t// Add headers specified by the HTTP header auth provider.\n\t\t\t\tif p.HttpHeader != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\tif p.HttpHeader.EmailHeader != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\t\t\theaders = append(headers, p.HttpHeader.EmailHeader)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\tif p.HttpHeader.UsernameHeader != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\t\t\theaders = append(headers, p.HttpHeader.UsernameHeader)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins is a list of headers that are safe to allow\n\t\t// even from untrusted clients. Importantly, this list does _not_ include\n\t\t// corsAllowHeader. The list is formatted for use with Access-Control-Allow-Headers.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace: indicates whether we should enable tracing for the request\n\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name: contains a client-reported name for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version: contains a client-reported version for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n\t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature: contains a client reported feature for the request source. The returned set should only include\n   145→\t// private repositories/project IDs.\n   146→\t//\n   147→\t// Because permissions fetching APIs are often expensive, the implementation should\n   148→\t// try to return partial but valid results in case of error, and it is up to callers\n   149→\t// to decide whether to discard.\n   150→\tFetchUserPerms(ctx context.Context, account *extsvc.Account, opts FetchPermsOptions) (*ExternalUserPermissions, error)\n   151→\n   152→\t// FetchRepoPerms returns a list of user IDs (on code host) who have read access to\n   153→\t// the given repository/project on the code host. the updates have been applied.\n//\n// At a high level, it does the following:\n//  1. Determine the identity of the user by applying the following rules in order:\n//     a. If ctx contains an authenticated Actor, the Actor's identity is the user identity.\n//     b. It must\n// also ensure that the user identity implied by op is consistent. in LIFO order. At the outermost layer: IP allowlist → tenant resolution → instrumentation/tracing → anonymous UID → request client extraction → security headers (CORS). Per-route auth layers then apply: (1) HTTP Header Auth (httpheader.AuthMiddleware) reads proxy-set username/email headers to authenticate; (2) Access Token Auth (accesstoken.AccessTokenAuthMiddleware) validates token from query, basic auth, or Authorization header against the DB; (3) OAuth Token Auth (oauthtoken.OAuthTokenAuthMiddleware) validates Bearer tokens issued by Sourcegraph's internal IdP (Fosite-based OIDC/OAuth2 server); (4) Cookie Auth (session.CookieMiddlewareWithCSRFSafety for API, CookieMiddleware for app) reads Redis-backed session cookie, verifying user existence, session validity, and license grant. After authentication, AppRequireAuthMiddleware/APIRequireAuthMiddleware reject unauthenticated requests (with anonymous-access exceptions). API scope enforcement (apiscope.RequireScopes) validates token scopes. authz.PostAuthMiddleware enforces valid license for authenticated non-admin users. Authentication providers are registered via providers.RegisterProviderFactory and include: builtin username/password, GitHub OAuth, GitLab OAuth, Bitbucket Cloud OAuth, Bitbucket Server OAuth, Azure DevOps OAuth, HTTP Header, OpenID Connect, SAML, Sourcegraph Operator (SOAP, an OIDC variant), and Sourcegraph Accounts (SAMS). External sign-in/callback routes (/.auth/*) dispatch to provider-specific handlers. GetAndSaveUser (cmd/frontend/auth/user.go) is the central function that all providers call to look up or create a user and persist external account associations. Repository-level authorization uses a separate Provider interface (internal/authz/iface.go) with implementations for GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket Server, Bitbucket Cloud, Perforce, Gerrit, and Azure DevOps, assembled by NewAuthzProviderFactory (internal/authz/providers/authz.go) and registered via authz.Init (cmd/frontend/internal/authz/init.go). Sub-repository permissions (Perforce path-level ACLs) are handled by internal/authz/subrepoperms. The IdP service (cmd/frontend/internal/auth/idp) implements RFC 6749/7591/8628 OAuth2 and OIDC for Sourcegraph acting as an authorization server (issuing tokens to MCP and other clients).\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2458,"cache_read_input_tokens":82000,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2458,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":9,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a30d89df-e9cc-4e7e-ba3e-62f97022ee4e","uuid":"10762061-5f82-415e-8561-f2c7e7e768d4"}

in LIFO order. At the outermost layer: IP allowlist → tenant resolution → instrumentation/tracing → anonymous UID → request client extraction → security headers (CORS). Per-route auth layers then apply: (1) HTTP Header Auth (httpheader.AuthMiddleware) reads proxy-set username/email headers to authenticate; (2) Access Token Auth (accesstoken.AccessTokenAuthMiddleware) validates token from query, basic auth, or Authorization header against the DB; (3) OAuth Token Auth (oauthtoken.OAuthTokenAuthMiddleware) validates Bearer tokens issued by Sourcegraph's internal IdP (Fosite-based OIDC/OAuth2 server); (4) Cookie Auth (session.CookieMiddlewareWithCSRFSafety for API, CookieMiddleware for app) reads Redis-backed session cookie, verifying user existence, session validity, and license grant. After authentication, AppRequireAuthMiddleware/APIRequireAuthMiddleware reject unauthenticated requests (with anonymous-access exceptions). API scope enforcement (apiscope.RequireScopes) validates token scopes. authz.PostAuthMiddleware enforces valid license for authenticated non-admin users. Authentication providers are registered via providers.RegisterProviderFactory and include: builtin username/password, GitHub OAuth, GitLab OAuth, Bitbucket Cloud OAuth, Bitbucket Server OAuth, Azure DevOps OAuth, HTTP Header, OpenID Connect, SAML, Sourcegraph Operator (SOAP, an OIDC variant), and Sourcegraph Accounts (SAMS). GetAndSaveUser (cmd/frontend/auth/user.go) is the central function that all providers call to look up or create a user and persist external account associations. Sub-repository permissions (Perforce path-level ACLs) are handled by internal/authz/subrepoperms. The IdP service (cmd/frontend/internal/auth/idp) implements RFC 6749/7591/8628 OAuth2 and OIDC for Sourcegraph acting as an authorization server (issuing tokens to MCP and other clients).\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
